### Template A-3.2 — Feasibility Assessment

**Purpose:** Determine whether a selected software project can realistically be **planned, built, tested, released, and maintained**. It evaluates technology, resources, time, budget, skills, risks, operations, security, and maintenance capacity.

**Lifecycle:** Produced in **Phase 4 — Feasibility and Business Case**. This assessment supplies the feasibility evidence needed to complete the **funding signal** for **G3 — Project Selected**, together with the Business Case.

**Primary owner:** Project Owner (coordinates the review and records the feasibility recommendation).

**Supporting owners:**

| Role | Responsibility |
| --- | --- |
| Technical lead / architect | Technical feasibility, architecture complexity, integrations, stack fit. |
| Business reviewer | Funding, operational value, expected benefit. |
| Product / UX reviewer | User feasibility, workflow fit, usability and adoption risk. |
| Security / governance reviewer | Privacy, security, compliance. |
| Operations / DevOps reviewer | Deployment, infrastructure, monitoring, maintenance feasibility. |

Solo projects: one person may complete all sections; **assumptions must still be explicit**.

#### Required sections

1. Project Identification
2. Source Documents
3. Feasibility Summary
4. Technical Feasibility
5. Resource Feasibility
6. Schedule Feasibility
7. Financial / Business Feasibility
8. Operational Feasibility
9. Security, Privacy, and Compliance Feasibility
10. Integration and Dependency Feasibility
11. Maintenance Feasibility
12. Feasibility Rating Summary
13. Risk Summary
14. Assumptions and Open Questions
15. Feasibility Decision
16. Approval Status

#### Form body

##### 1. Project Identification

```text
Project Name:
Idea Title:
Project Owner:
Date Prepared:
Reviewer(s):
Lifecycle Phase: Phase 4 — Feasibility and Business Case
Existing Product ID (PRD-XXX), if any:
Candidate New Product? Yes / No / Unknown:
Candidate PCL Code (PCL-L.D.E.C):
PCL Criticality Rationale:
Domain Tags:
Function Descriptors:
Work Type Tag(s), if pre-product or cross-cutting:
```

##### 2. Source Documents

List documents used for this assessment.

```text
Source Documents:
- Idea Capture Form:
- Problem Definition Document:
- Project Selection Scorecard / evaluation record:
- Business Field Report (Template A-4):
- Early Research Notes:
- Technical Notes:
- Stakeholder Notes:
- Other:
```

At minimum, reference the **Idea Capture Form**, **Problem Definition Document**, and **Phase 3** selection evidence (**Project Selection Scorecard** and/or **Business Field Report** per program rules).

##### 3. Feasibility Summary

```text
Overall Feasibility Summary:
```

Consider: Does the project appear realistic? What helps feasibility? What hurts it? What must be clarified before proceeding?

##### 4. Technical Feasibility

Evaluate whether the project can be built with available or acceptable technology.

```text
Technical Feasibility:

Required technologies:
Known technology stack:
New tools or frameworks required:
Architecture complexity:
Data storage needs:
API requirements:
Performance needs:
Security needs:
Prototype required? Yes / No
Technical unknowns:
```

| Technical Feasibility Rating | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| High | Technology known, available, realistic. |
| Medium | Feasible with technical unknowns. |
| Low | Significant technical barriers. |
| Unknown | More technical research required. |

##### 5. Resource Feasibility

```text
Resource Feasibility:

Required roles:
Available skills:
Missing skills:

Required licenses:
Required vendors:
Development capacity:
Support capacity:
```

| Resource Feasibility Rating | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| High | People, skills, tools available. |
| Medium | Gaps manageable. |
| Low | Major gaps. |
| Unknown | Needs unclear. |

##### 6. Schedule Feasibility

```text
Schedule Feasibility:

Desired start date:
Desired release date:
Estimated duration:
Major milestones:
Time-sensitive deadlines:
Schedule risks:
Dependencies affecting timeline:
```

| Schedule Feasibility Rating | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| High | Timeline realistic. |
| Medium | Realistic with scope discipline. |
| Low | Likely unrealistic. |
| Unknown | Cannot estimate. |

##### 7. Financial / Business Feasibility

```text
Financial / Business Feasibility:

Estimated cost:
Expected savings:
Expected revenue:
Expected efficiency gain:
Expected customer value:
Funding availability:
Return on investment:
Cost of not doing the project:
```

Use **Template A-5** for structured forecasts when appropriate.

| Financial / Business Feasibility Rating | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| High | Strong value vs cost. |
| Medium | Reasonable; needs validation. |
| Low | Cost may exceed value. |
| Unknown | Financial picture unclear. |

##### 8. Operational Feasibility

```text
Operational Feasibility:

Who will use it?
Who will administer it?
Who will support it?
What workflow will change?
Training needed?
Documentation needed?
Support load impact?
Fit with current operations?
```

| Operational Feasibility Rating | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| High | Fits operations well. |
| Medium | Process change / training needed. |
| Low | Major disruption likely. |
| Unknown | Impact unclear. |

##### 9. Security, Privacy, and Compliance Feasibility

```text

```

| Security / Compliance Feasibility Rating | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| High | Requirements clear and manageable. |
| Medium | Reviews or controls required. |
| Low | Major barriers. |
| Unknown | Needs investigation. |

##### 10. Integration and Dependency Feasibility

```text

```

| Integration Feasibility Rating | Meaning |
| --- | --- |

| Medium | Some uncertainty. |
| Low | Critical dependencies risky. |

```text

Expected maintenance owner:
Support level:

```

| Maintenance Feasibility Rating | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| High | Manageable. |
| Medium | Manageable with planning. |
| Low | Burden may be too high. |
| Unknown | Unclear. |

##### 12. Feasibility Rating Summary

| Feasibility area | Rating | Notes |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Technical | | |
| Resource | | |
| Schedule | | |
| Financial / Business | | |
| Operational | | |
| Security / Privacy / Compliance | | |
| Integration / Dependency | | |
| Maintenance | | |

##### 13. Risk Summary

```text
Major Risks:
-
Risk Mitigations:
-
Blocking Risks:
-
Non-Blocking Risks:
-
```

Blocking risks must be resolved or owned before continuing. Non-blocking risks may be monitored or mitigated in later phases.

##### 14. Assumptions and Open Questions

```text
Assumptions:
-
Open Questions:
-
Required Research:
```

Feasibility often rests on early assumptions, so anything that could change approval must be visible.

##### 15. Feasibility Decision

```text
Feasibility Decision:
Decision Date:
Decision Maker:
Decision Rationale:
Required Follow-Up:
Next Lifecycle Phase:
```

| Decision | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Feasible | Supports proceeding to requirements. |
| Feasible with conditions | Supports proceeding only when named conditions are owned. |
| Pivot recommended | Feasible only if direction changes. |
| Research required | More investigation first. |
| Not feasible now | Defer. |
| Not feasible | Stop. |

##### 16. Approval Status

```text
Approval Status:
Reviewer:
Review Date:
Decision Notes:
```

| Status | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Draft | Still being prepared. |
| Submitted | Submitted for review. |
| Under Review | In review. |
| Feasible — Proceed to Requirements | Feasible and funded enough to proceed to Phase 5. |
| Conditionally Feasible — Proceed to Requirements | Proceed to Phase 5 only with recorded conditions and owners. |
| Pivot | Direction should change before requirements work. |
| Deferred | Not feasible now. |
| Stopped | Should not continue. |

#### Completion criteria

The Feasibility Assessment is complete when:

1. Project is identified and **source documents** listed.
2. **Overall summary** recorded.
3. Sections **4–11** evaluated with ratings (or explicit Unknown + plan).
4. **Rating summary** filled.
5. **Risks** and mitigations documented (blocking vs non-blocking).
6. **Assumptions** and **open questions** listed.
7. **Feasibility decision** and **approval status** recorded.

Incomplete if major areas are blank, risks ignored, assumptions hidden, or no decision recorded.

### Template A-3.3 — Business Case

**Purpose:** Package the funding recommendation for **Phase 4 — Feasibility and Business Case** using feasibility findings, projected benefits, costs, risks, constraints, and decision conditions. The Business Case supplies the funding evidence needed to complete **G3 — Project Selected**, together with the Feasibility Assessment.

**Required inputs:**

- Project Selection Scorecard (Template A-3.1) or equivalent evaluation record.
- Business Field Report (Template A-4) or approved waiver.
- Feasibility Assessment (Template A-3.2).
- Forecast / projection workbook or assumptions (Template A-5) when economic viability depends on modeled projections.

#### Required sections

1. Executive Summary
2. Strategic Alignment
3. Expected Benefits
4. Expected Costs / Investment
5. ROI, Payback, or Scenario Summary
6. Major Risks and Mitigations
7. Constraints and Dependencies
8. PRCS Product Classification Summary
9. Recommendation
10. Conditions
11. Approval Record

#### Form body

##### 1. Executive Summary

```text
Executive Summary:
```

Provide the recommendation in one paragraph.

##### 2. Strategic Alignment

```text
Strategic Alignment:
```

Explain how the initiative supports portfolio, product, customer, compliance, or operational priorities.

##### 3. Expected Benefits

```text
Expected Benefits:
```

Quantify benefits where possible (revenue, savings, risk reduction, productivity, customer experience, compliance posture).

##### 4. Expected Costs / Investment

```text
Expected Costs / Investment:
```

Include delivery effort, infrastructure, vendors, licenses, operational support, maintenance, and change-management costs where known.

##### 5. ROI, Payback, or Scenario Summary

```text
ROI / Payback / Scenario Summary:
Forecast Reference (Template A-5, if used):
```

Use Template A-5 when economic viability depends on modeled revenue, expense, cash, or market assumptions.

##### 6. Major Risks and Mitigations

```text
Major Risks:
Risk Mitigations:
```

Risks should align with the Feasibility Assessment and include owners when mitigation is required before proceeding.

##### 7. Constraints and Dependencies

```text
Constraints:
Dependencies:
```

Include funding, capacity, vendor, security/privacy/compliance, integration, timeline, or operational constraints.

##### 8. PRCS Product Classification Summary

```text
Existing Product ID (PRD-XXX), if any:
Candidate / Approved Product ID:
Candidate PCL Code (PCL-L.D.E.C):
PCL Criticality Tier:
Domain Tags:
Function Descriptors:
Work Type Tag(s), if pre-product or cross-cutting:

Downstream Standards Tiering Impact:
```

Use this section to preserve the G3 PRCS candidate decision. Final production registration is confirmed at G8.

##### 9. Recommendation

```text
Recommendation: (Proceed to Requirements | Proceed to Requirements with Conditions | Pivot | Defer | Stop)
Recommendation Rationale:
```

##### 10. Conditions

```text
Conditions (if any):
Condition Owner(s):
Due Date(s):
```

Conditions are required when recommending a conditional proceed.

##### 11. Approval Record

```text
Approved By:
Role / Authority:
Date:
Decision Notes:
```

#### Completion criteria

The Business Case is complete when the recommendation is explicit, costs and benefits are traceable to assumptions (and **Template A-5** when used), risks are visible, constraints/dependencies are documented, any conditions have owners and due dates, and the approver and date are recorded.

---

### Template A-4 — Business Field Report

**Purpose:** Analyze a **business field** (market, industry, or opportunity space) so the organization can make **informed portfolio and funding decisions**. Standard sections support **Phase 3 — Project Evaluation and Selection** and inform **Phase 4 — Feasibility and Business Case**.

**Audience:** Tailor depth and tone to executives, sponsors, product leadership, or portfolio reviewers—state the intended audience in the introduction.

**Quality bar:** Credible sources, clear citations, concise narrative, visuals where they clarify quant trends, and **specific recommendations** tied to evidence.

#### Core sections (outline)

| Section | Content |
| --- | --- |
| **Executive summary** | Findings, conclusions, and recommendations (standalone readable). |
| **Introduction** | Field definition, scope, relevance to the organization. |
| **Market analysis** | Size, growth, segmentation, trends; demographics and customer profiles; behavior (needs, buying habits, brand perception); primary vs secondary research methods; benefits of structured market research. |
| **Competitive analysis** | Major players, share, strategies; strengths/weaknesses; differentiation / USP; **financial view** (statements, ratios, benchmarking, trends)—see Financial analysis subset below. |
| **Future outlook** | Forecast trends; recommendations for players in the space. |
| **SWOT** | Strengths, weaknesses, opportunities, threats for the **industry or opportunity context**; prioritize factors; derive strategies, options, resource focus, and risk responses. |
| **Trends and challenges** | Notable drivers (technology, digital transformation, ESG, globalization, remote work, data-driven decisions, CX) and pressures (economy, supply chain, cyber, talent, regulation, climate, geopolitical risk). |
| **Potential growth areas** | Innovation, expansion, technology, operational excellence, CX, sustainability/ESG; techniques (research, SWOT, scenarios, workshops, customer feedback). |
| **Recommendations** | Aligned to goals, feasible, measurable, risk-aware, prioritized—product/service, markets, operations, CX, digital, sustainability as relevant. |
| **Conclusion** | Restate main conclusions and next decisions. |

#### Financial analysis subset (within competitive or industry analysis)

Use when public or internal financial data exists for relevant companies:

1. Gather statements (income, balance sheet, cash flow).
2. Compute ratios: profitability (e.g. gross/net margin, ROE, ROA), liquidity (current, quick), solvency (debt-to-equity, interest coverage), efficiency (inventory and receivables turnover, as applicable).
3. Benchmark against peers and industry norms.
4. Trend over periods; interpret with judgment.

#### Specialized variants (reuse the same evidence standards)

**Market entry analysis** — Assess entering a new geography or segment: market assessment; regulatory/IP; economics (macro, FX, infrastructure); culture and behavior; entry modes (export, licensing, franchise, JV, FDI, etc.); risk (political, economic, currency, operational).

**Emerging technology report** — Identify and assess technologies: maturity, feasibility and viability, market potential, competitive landscape, regulation, ethics, future outlook and organizational implications.

**Customer segmentation study** — Demographic, psychographic, behavioral, needs-based segments; steps: collect data → analyze → identify segments → profile → prioritize.

**Competitive landscape analysis** — Direct vs indirect competitors; share and strategies; SWOT per competitor where useful; customer and financial views; outlook and implications.

---

### Template A-5 — Entrepreneurial forecasting guide

**Purpose:** Document **defensible financial and market projections** for **Phase 4 — Feasibility and Business Case** (economic feasibility, cash and runway) and establish habits for **actual-vs-forecast** review in **Phase 13 — Maintenance and Improvement**.

**Scope:** Revenue, expenses, cash timing, market trend assumptions, growth scenarios—not a substitute for statutory accounting or audited statements.

#### What to estimate

| Area | Typical questions |
| --- | --- |
| Revenue | Income scale and timing (subscriptions, usage, services). |
| Expenses | People, infrastructure, sales/marketing, tooling, overhead. |
| Market trends | Demand, competition, regulation. |
| Growth | Customers, usage, expansion paths. |

#### Why forecasting matters

- Capital and runway planning  
- Risk surfacing and mitigation  
- Sponsor or investor alignment  
- Hiring, pricing, and roadmap decisions  
- Benchmarks for **later** performance evaluation (Phase 13)  

#### Types

| Type | Focus |
| --- | --- |
| Sales | Pipeline and historical conversion to future periods. |
| Expense | Fixed and variable costs by category. |
| Cash flow | When cash moves—not only accrual profit. |
| Market | External shifts affecting demand or compliance costs. |

#### Methods

| Approach | When |
| --- | --- |
| **Qualitative** | Sparse history—expert input, customer research, **scenario planning** (what-if cases). |
| **Quantitative** | Reliable history—trends, smoothing (e.g. moving averages), regression between drivers (e.g. marketing spend and qualified leads). |

#### Steps

1. **Define goals** — Metrics and horizon (monthly / quarterly / annual).  
2. **Gather data** — Internal actuals and external benchmarks.  
3. **Choose methods** — Match data maturity and uncertainty.  
4. **State assumptions** — Seasonality, pricing, competition, regulatory steps; prefer documented ranges.  
5. **Build scenarios** — At minimum **best**, **likely**, and **worst** cases tied to named drivers.  
6. **Monitor and revise** — Compare actuals on a cadence; update models when reality diverges (handoff to Phase 13).  

#### Tooling (examples)

Spreadsheets; accounting systems for actuals; forecasting/planning apps; CRM or billing analytics for revenue drivers—pick tools your finance and ops teams can sustain.

#### Common mistakes

Overstated revenue; ignored taxes, inflation, or step costs; frozen forecasts despite market change; weak competitor/regulatory awareness; intuition without data checks.

#### Practices

Start with tractable horizons; segment by product, region, or customer where material; involve cross-functional inputs; use industry benchmarks where valid; reserve contingency scenarios for shocks.

---

### Template A-6 — Scope Document

**Purpose:** Establish the approved project boundary for the current planning horizon: what is included, what is excluded, what is deferred, and what assumptions or constraints govern delivery. The Scope Document supports **Phase 6 — Planning and Scope Control** and change control.

**Required inputs:**

- Approved or baselined requirements package (CRS/SRS or equivalent).
- Business Case (Template A-3.3).
- Feasibility Assessment (Template A-3.2).
- Stakeholder and User Profile (SUP-001) when stakeholder authority or user groups affect scope.

#### Required sections

1. Project Identification
2. Scope Summary
3. In-Scope Outcomes
4. Out-of-Scope Items
5. Deferred Items
6. Assumptions
7. Constraints
8. Dependencies
9. Acceptance / Success Boundaries
10. Change Control Notes
11. Approval Record

#### Form body

##### 1. Project Identification

```text
Project Name:
Project Owner:
Date Prepared:
Prepared By:
Reviewer(s):
Lifecycle Phase: Phase 6 — Planning and Scope Control
```

##### 2. Scope Summary

```text
Scope Summary:
```

Describe the planning horizon and the intended delivery boundary in plain language.

##### 3. In-Scope Outcomes

```text
In-Scope Outcomes:
```

List outcomes, capabilities, features, workstreams, or deliverables included in the baseline.

##### 4. Out-of-Scope Items

```text
Out-of-Scope Items:
```

List items explicitly excluded so they cannot silently enter the plan.

##### 5. Deferred Items

```text
Deferred Items:
```

List valid items that are not included in the current planning horizon.

##### 6. Assumptions

```text
Assumptions:
```

Record assumptions that affect scope, capacity, timing, users, vendors, data, or compliance.

##### 7. Constraints

```text

```

Include budget, schedule, regulatory, technical, staffing, vendor, platform, or operational constraints.

##### 8. Dependencies

```text

```

List dependent teams, systems, vendors, approvals, environments, data, or decisions.

##### 9. Acceptance / Success Boundaries


Define how the team knows the scoped work is complete enough for the planning horizon.

##### 10. Change Control Notes

```text

```

State how scope changes are requested, evaluated, approved, deferred, or rejected.

##### 11. Approval Record

```text
Approved By:
Role / Authority:
Approval Date:
Decision Notes:
```

#### Completion criteria

The Scope Document is complete when in-scope outcomes, out-of-scope items, deferred items, assumptions, constraints, dependencies, acceptance boundaries, change-control notes, and approval record are documented. It is incomplete if major exclusions are implicit or if decision authority is unclear.

### Template A-9 — Feature Inventory Document

**Purpose:** List, organize, and classify **planned software features** for a project. The Feature Inventory Document creates a controlled feature list that connects scope, requirements, design, development, testing, and release planning, reducing duplicated functionality, silent scope growth, and missing traceability.

**Lifecycle:** Produced or refreshed in **Phase 6 — Planning and Scope Control** when the program tracks capabilities at feature granularity.

**Primary owner:** Project Owner (maintains the official list and ensures each feature has purpose, priority, owner, and lifecycle status).

**Supporting reviewers:**

| Role | Responsibility |
| --- | --- |
| Product / business reviewer | Confirms business value and priority. |
| Technical lead / architect | Confirms feasibility and technical dependencies. |
| UI/UX reviewer | Confirms user workflow and interface impact. |
| QA / tester | Confirms testability and acceptance needs. |
| Security / governance reviewer | Flags security, privacy, compliance, access-control concerns. |

#### Required sections

1. Project Identification
2. Source Documents
3. Feature Inventory Summary
4. Feature Classification Rules
5. Feature Priority Rules
6. Feature Status Rules
7. Feature Inventory Table
8. Feature Dependency Summary
9. Out-of-Scope Feature List
10. Risk and Complexity Notes
11. Traceability Notes
12. Approval Status

#### Form body

##### 1. Project Identification

```text
Project Name:
Project Owner:
Date Prepared:
Last Updated:
Reviewer(s):
Lifecycle Phase: Phase 6 — Planning and Scope Control
```

##### 2. Source Documents

```text
Source Documents:
- Idea Capture Form:
- Problem Definition Document:
- Project Selection Scorecard:
- Feasibility Assessment:
- Business Case:
- Requirements Specification Package:
- Customer Requirements Specification:
- Software Requirements Specification:
- Scope Document:
- UI/UX Notes:
- Stakeholder Notes:
- Other:
```

##### 3. Feature Inventory Summary

```text
Feature Inventory Summary:
```

Helpful questions: What major capabilities are included? Which goals do they support? What is essential for the first release? What is later? What is explicitly excluded?

##### 4. Feature Classification Rules

| Feature type | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Core | Essential for the product to work. |
| Supporting | Helps complete core workflows. |
| Administrative | Admins, managers, maintainers. |
| Integration | External or internal system connections. |
| Reporting | Dashboards, analytics, exports. |
| Security | Access, data protection, behavior controls. |
| Compliance | Policy, legal, regulatory, audit. |
| Convenience | Improves UX; not required for basic operation. |
| Future | Useful later; not in current release. |

##### 5. Feature Priority Rules

| Priority | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Must have | Required for first usable release. |
| Should have | Important but not blocking first release. |
| Could have | If time and resources allow. |
| Won't have now | Explicitly out of current release. |
| Future | Planned or possible later. |

Shorthand: **MUST** · **SHOULD** · **COULD** · **WONT** · **FUTURE**

##### 6. Feature Status Rules

| Status | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Proposed | Suggested; not approved. |
| Approved | Approved for planning. |
| Designed | Design or architecture defined. |
| Ready for development | Requirements and design sufficient to build. |
| In development | Being built. |
| In testing | Under test / validation. |
| Complete | Passed required checks. |
| Deferred | Moved to a future release. |
| Rejected | Will not be built. |
| Removed | Was planned; removed from scope. |

##### 7. Feature Inventory Table

| Feature ID | Feature Name | Description | Type | Priority | Status | Target Users | Related Requirement(s) | Dependencies | Complexity | Notes |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| FEAT-001 | | | | | | | | | | |

**Feature ID format:** sequential `FEAT-001`, `FEAT-002`, etc. For larger systems, prefix by module: `AUTH-FEAT-001`, `BILL-FEAT-001`, etc.

##### 8. Feature Dependency Summary

```text
Feature Dependencies:
-
External Dependencies:
-
Technical Dependencies:
-
Design Dependencies:
-
Data Dependencies:
-
Security / Compliance Dependencies:
-
```

##### 9. Out-of-Scope Feature List

| Feature Name | Reason Excluded | Possible Future Phase | Notes |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| | | | |

##### 10. Risk and Complexity Notes

```text
High-Complexity Features:
-
High-Risk Features:
-
Features Needing Research:
-
Features Needing Prototype:
-
Features With Security / Privacy Concerns:
-
```

##### 11. Traceability Notes

Each approved feature should trace to at least one **requirement**, **problem**, **user need**, or **business objective**.

```text
Traceability Notes:
```

Minimum path: **Problem → Requirement → Feature → Design → Code → Test → Release**

| Feature ID | Traces Back To | Evidence |
| --- | --- | --- |
| FEAT-001 | REQ-001 | Requirement describes login. |

##### 12. Approval Status

```text
Approval Status:
Reviewer:
Review Date:
Decision Notes:
```

| Status | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Draft | Inventory still being prepared. |
| Submitted | Submitted for review. |
| Under Review | Review in progress. |
| Approved | Accepted as scope baseline for planning horizon. |
| Approved with Conditions | Accepted after stated corrections. |
| Needs Revision | Must correct before approval. |
| Deferred | Review postponed. |
| Rejected | Not acceptable in current form. |

#### Completion criteria

The Feature Inventory Document is complete when project identification and source documents are recorded; classification, priority, and status rules are defined; every known in-scope feature appears with a unique ID, name, description, type, priority, status, users where applicable, requirement links or explicit gaps, dependencies, and complexity; out-of-scope candidates are listed with rationale; risks, complexity, and traceability notes are updated; and approval status is assigned by a named reviewer with date.

### Template A-10 — Non-Functional Requirements Document

The canonical non-functional requirements template is maintained as **`Non-Functional Requirements — NFR-001.md`**, especially **§9 — Template — Non-Functional Requirements Document**.

**Purpose:** Capture measurable quality attributes, constraints, and operating expectations for **Phase 5 — Requirements Definition** and align them to SRS non-functional requirements (`SRS-NFR-...`) before **G4 — Requirements Approved**.

Do not duplicate the full template here; use NFR-001 as the controlled source.

# Appendix B — Checklists

This appendix is the supplementary **UI/UX checklist library** for the Master Lifecycle. It does not replace lifecycle-wide quality/compliance checks in **`25. Quality and Compliance Checks.md`** or normative USSM Annex E checklists.

Normative compliance review checklists for SRS, design, and testing remain in **USSM Section 10.5 — Annex E**. This appendix holds UI/UX scoring and audit criteria for design reviews (Phase 7) and experiential QA (Phase 10).

**Layout patterns (CRM / admin):** For concrete shell structure (global containers, 12-column grid, sidebar + content, master–detail, modal overlay, section wireframes for lists/dashboard/RBAC/CMS), use **`UI-UX Layout Guide — LYG-001.md`** in addition to the scoring tables below.

---

## UI/UX Scoring Criteria and Audit Framework

**Classification:** Keep — standalone Appendix B UI/UX scoring and audit framework for visual hierarchy, consistency, feedback, typography, usability heuristics, information architecture, accessibility, and task-friction metrics.

When evaluating **UI** (visual and interactive surface), criteria emphasize **how it looks and responds**, balancing aesthetics with functional clarity.

### UI — Visual hierarchy and composition

| Topic | What to score |
| --- | --- |
| **Contrast** | Text and controls meet readability targets (e.g. WCAG 2.1 — commonly **4.5:1** for normal body text unless a conformant exception applies). |
| **Whitespace** | Enough negative space to avoid cognitive overload vs. cluttered layouts. |
| **Fitts’s law** | Primary actions are easy to acquire—adequate target size and placement. |

### UI — Consistency and standardized patterns

| Topic | What to score |
| --- | --- |
| **Component reuse** | Buttons, inputs, icons follow one system across screens. |
| **Internal consistency** | Repeated patterns (e.g. cancel/destructive placement) stay predictable. |
| **External consistency** | Alignment with platform conventions (e.g. Material Design, Apple Human Interface Guidelines) where applicable. |

### UI — Interactive feedback (“feel”)

| Topic | What to score |
| --- | --- |
| **Affordances** | Interactive elements read as interactive (buttons, links, tappable areas). |
| **States** | Clear cues for hover, active, disabled, loading. |
| **Perceived responsiveness** | Immediate acknowledgment (~**100 ms** perceived feedback) even when backend work is slower. |

### UI — Typography and readability

| Topic | What to score |
| --- | --- |
| **Hierarchy** | Distinct roles for headings vs. body vs. secondary text. |
| **Measure and rhythm** | Comfortable line length (often ~**45–75** characters per line for body copy) and spacing. |

### Quick UI audit scorecard (example dimensions)

| UI attribute | Goal | Example metric |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Aesthetics | Professionalism and brand fit | Subjective rating (e.g. 1–10) |
| Accessibility | Inclusivity | Contrast / typography pass–fail vs. policy |
| Efficiency | Speed of interaction | Click/tap accuracy in moderated tasks |
| Clarity | Reduced confusion | Icon or label recognition |
| Feedback | System status | Loading/error/success patterns present |

---

## UX — Journey, friction, and structure

**UX** separates **logic, friction, and emotion** of the journey from pure visuals.

### Core usability (heuristic lens)

Score severity of issues (e.g. **0–4**) across typical heuristic themes:

- **Recognition vs. recall** — Is needed information visible vs. memorized across steps?
- **Flexibility and efficiency** — Shortcuts for experts without harming novices?
- **Error prevention** — Guardrails before destructive or irreversible actions?
- **User control and freedom** — Undo, escape paths, recoverability?

### Information architecture (IA)

| Measure | Intent |
| --- | --- |
| **Tree testing** | Users can find targets from navigation labels alone (text-only IA probe). |
| **Card sorting agreement** | Categories match user mental models. |
| **Search vs. navigation** | Heavy immediate search use may signal navigation or labeling gaps. |

### Experience qualities (Morville honeycomb)

Useful · Usable · Desirable · Findable · Accessible · Credible · Valuable — qualitative scoring across facets as appropriate to the product.

### Interaction / friction metrics

| Metric | Signal |
| --- | --- |
| **Task satisfaction / mental effort** | E.g. single-task effort rating after representative tasks. |
| **Back navigation usage** | Elevated “back” use may indicate confusion or wrong paths. |
| **Pogo-sticking** | Search/catalog: click result → immediate return → another result suggests relevance or preview gaps. |

### UI vs. UX emphasis (same surface, different lens)

| Element | UI emphasis | UX emphasis |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Button | Visual treatment, affordance | User understands outcome before acting |
| Form | Legibility, density | Field count, flow, errors recoverable |
| Navigation | Visual cleanliness | Primary destinations discoverable |
| Error | Styling, visibility | Message explains fix or next step |

**Specialized systems** (e.g. dense dashboards): often weight **efficiency** and **error prevention** highest.

---

## Related

- `USSM — Unified Software Standards Manual v1.0.md` — Annex E compliance checklists.
- `25. Quality and Compliance Checks.md` — lifecycle quality/compliance map and USSM Annex E mapping.
- `13. Phase 7 — Architecture and Design.md` — UI/UX design review.
- `16. Phase 10 — Testing and Validation.md` — experiential and UI acceptance checks.






# Appendix C — Scoring Models

## 1. Purpose

This appendix collects scoring models used by the Master Lifecycle. Scores support decisions; they do not replace gate approvals, required evidence, named accountability, or professional judgment.

Use scoring to:

- compare candidate initiatives,
- classify complexity and review depth,
- prioritize scope, features, risks, defects, changes, and improvements,
- support release readiness and compliance decisions,
- make tradeoffs explicit and auditable.

## 2. Scoring Principles

- Define criteria before scoring.
- Record evidence links for each material score.
- Use the same scale consistently within one decision.
- Document weights when criteria are not equal.
- Treat unknowns as risk, not as zero.
- Preserve reviewer, date, rationale, and decision outcome.
- Use higher rigor when complexity, criticality, data sensitivity, security, privacy, compliance, or operational exposure requires it.

## 3. Common Scale

Use a 1–5 scale unless a template or program defines another scale.

| Score | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| 1 | Weak / low fit / high concern |
| 2 | Limited / below expectations |
| 3 | Acceptable / moderate / baseline |
| 4 | Strong / low concern |
| 5 | Excellent / high confidence |

For risk, use likelihood × impact where appropriate:

| Risk score | Severity |
| --- | --- |
| 1–4 | Low |
| 5–9 | Medium |
| 10–16 | High |
| 17–25 | Critical |

## 4. Project Selection Scoring

Use **Template A-3.1 — Project Selection Scorecard** for Phase 3 selection. Criteria may include:

| Criterion | Typical weight | Notes |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Strategic alignment | 10–20% | Fit with product, customer, operational, or compliance goals. |
| Customer / user value | 10–20% | Pain severity, reach, usability or support value. |
| Business value | 10–20% | Revenue, savings, retention, risk reduction, efficiency. |
| Feasibility | 10–20% | Technical, staffing, schedule, dependency confidence. |
| Risk / compliance exposure | 10–20% | Lower risk scores higher unless risk reduction is the goal. |
| Urgency / timing | 5–15% | Deadline, market window, regulatory or operational pressure. |
| Maintainability / operational fit | 5–15% | Support cost, observability, ownership, lifecycle fit. |

Recommended formula:

```text
Weighted Score = Sum(score x weight)
```

The scorecard is a selection signal only. **G3 — Project Selected** is not complete until Phase 4 adds feasibility and business-case evidence.

## 5. Complexity and Criticality Scoring

Use **`23. Project Complexity Levels.md`** for the canonical Small / Medium / Large / Unknown rubric.

Scoring can help assign the level:

| Driver | Low / Small | Medium | Large / High |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Users / reach | Few internal users | Multiple groups | Broad customer or tenant reach |
| Data sensitivity | Public/internal only | Some confidential data | PII, regulated, restricted, tenant-sensitive |
| Integrations | None or simple | Several known integrations | Complex, external, business-critical integrations |
| Availability | Low impact downtime | Moderate operational impact | High availability or SLA/SLO commitments |
| Security / compliance | Basic controls | Security/privacy review needed | Regulated, authz, tenant isolation, audit-heavy |
| Delivery uncertainty | Known path | Some unknowns | Major unknowns or high dependency risk |

Criticality overrides complexity. A small change can require high rigor if it affects regulated data, security controls, auth/authz, production infrastructure, customer commitments, or release posture.

## 6. MoSCoW / Priority Scoring

Use for scope, feature inventory, maintenance backlog, improvement recommendations, and release decisions.

| Priority | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Must | Required for gate, release, compliance, safety, or committed scope. |
| Should | Important but can be deferred with accepted impact. |
| Could | Valuable if capacity allows. |
| Won't / Not now | Explicitly out of current scope or deferred. |

Alternative priority codes:

| Code | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| P0 | Blocks release, deployment, support, or critical operation. |
| P1 | Needed in current cycle. |
| P2 | Planned follow-up. |
| P3 | Optional / observation. |

## 7. Change and Defect Risk Scoring

Use likelihood × impact for change requests, defects, incidents, and release blockers.

| Impact factor | Considerations |
| --- | --- |
| Customer impact | Number of users, severity of workflow disruption, support burden. |
| Data impact | Loss, corruption, privacy, retention, tenant isolation, migration risk. |
| Security impact | Auth/authz, secrets, vulnerabilities, exposure, abuse potential. |
| Operational impact | Availability, rollback difficulty, observability, incident likelihood. |
| Compliance impact | Contractual, regulatory, audit, or policy obligations. |

Risk treatment should align with **`26. Change Control.md`** and relevant gate evidence.

## 8. Testing and Release Readiness Scoring

For **G7** and **G8**, scores should support pass/fail/conditional decisions.

| Area | Example signal |
| --- | --- |
| Test execution | Planned vs run vs passed, blocked tests, waived tests. |
| Defects | Open critical/high count, deferred defects, verification status. |
| Coverage | Requirement coverage, unit/integration/system/acceptance coverage. |
| CI/CD health | Build stability, static analysis, security/accessibility checks. |
| Release readiness | Known issues, rollback confidence, support readiness, security review. |

Release should not be approved on aggregate score alone when critical blockers exist.

## 9. UI/UX Scoring

Use **`29. Appendix B — Checklists.md`** for UI/UX scoring. Common dimensions include:

- visual hierarchy,
- consistency,
- feedback and states,
- typography/readability,
- accessibility,
- information architecture,
- usability heuristics,
- task friction.

UI/UX findings should map to requirements, defects, or improvement recommendations.

## 10. CYBERCUBE Release / Compliance Scoring

When product classification, criticality, or release policy requires CYBERCUBE release scoring, use the CYBERCUBE compliance matrix:

- 9 dimensions, 0–5 each, maximum 45.
- **>= 40**: Release-grade.
- **32–39**: Conditional; remediation required.
- **< 32**: Blocked.

Dimensions:

| Dimension | Focus |
| --- | --- |
| Content | Clarity, terminology, versioned copy. |
| Yield | KPIs, measurable value, post-launch validation. |
| Brand | Voice, tone, naming, visual rules. |
| Engagement | CTAs, progressive disclosure, interaction signals. |
| Responsiveness | Multi-device, accessibility, performance. |
| Conversion | Funnels, forms, drop-off analysis. |
| UX | IA, recovery paths, research-based usability. |
| Backend | Security, scalability, observability. |
| Experience | Trust, onboarding/offboarding, support transparency. |

This score can support **G8 — Release Approved** but does not replace required release evidence.

## 11. Recording Scores

Every scoring record should include:

```text
Scoring model:
Criteria:
Weights:
Scores:
Evidence links:
Reviewer(s):
Date:
Recommendation:
Decision / gate link:
Assumptions:
Unknowns:
```

## 12. Related Documents

- **`09. Phase 3 — Project Evaluation and Selection.md`** — project selection scoring.
- **`23. Project Complexity Levels.md`** — complexity and criticality scaling.
- **`25. Quality and Compliance Checks.md`** — lifecycle quality/compliance map.
- **`26. Change Control.md`** — change and risk classification.
- **`29. Appendix B — Checklists.md`** — UI/UX scoring.
- **`28. Appendix A — Template Library.md`** — Template A-3.1 and related scoring/evidence templates.
- CYBERCUBE compliance matrix — release-grade scoring model.






# Appendix D — CYBERCUBE Standards Applicability Matrix

## 1. Purpose

This appendix is the reusable evidence form for determining which CYBERCUBE standards apply to a project, why they apply, what evidence is required, and which lifecycle gates must confirm that evidence.

Use this appendix with `25. Quality and Compliance Checks.md` §5. That section defines the core applicability rules; this appendix provides the project-level record.

---

## 2. Lifecycle Role

| Lifecycle point | Use |
| --- | --- |
| Phase 4 / G3 | Identify high-risk applicable standards before funding or selection proceeds. |
| Phase 5 / G4 | Convert applicable standards into requirements, NFRs, constraints, and acceptance criteria. |
| Phase 7 / G5 | Reflect standards in architecture, data, API, security, privacy, observability, UX, and integration designs. |
| Phase 8 / G6 | Prepare tools, CI, coding standards, environments, test setup, and evidence controls. |
| Phase 11 / G8 | Confirm standards evidence is complete or non-applicability rationale is approved before release. |
| Phase 14 / G10 | Review gaps, exceptions, evidence quality, and next-cycle improvements. |

---

## 3. Applicability Record

```text
Project Name:
Product / Service:
Product ID (PRD-XXX, if assigned):
PCL Code (PCL-L.D.E.C, candidate or approved):
PCL Status: Candidate / Approved / Not Yet Applicable
Domain Tags:
Function Descriptors:
Work Type Tag(s), if pre-product or cross-cutting:
Product Owner:
Prepared By:
Reviewer(s):
Date Prepared:
Lifecycle Phase First Completed:
Last Reviewed:
```

---

## 4. Applicability Matrix

| Standard / Policy | Trigger | Applies? | Rationale | Evidence Required | Gate Check | Owner | Status |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| PRCS Product Classification | Any production product; candidate product selected for feasibility; architectural change affecting PCL facets; pre-product or cross-cutting work needing Work Type Tags | Yes / No / Conditional | | Candidate PCL at G3; approved `PRD-XXX` + `PCL-L.D.E.C` before production release at G8; Work Type Tag(s) for pre-product or cross-cutting work where no PRD exists | G3 / G8 | Product Owner | |
| Naming & Identifier Standard (`STD-ENG-001`) | Any project producing lifecycle artifacts, governance records, public entity IDs, APIs/logs/URLs, modules, components, files, or release evidence | Yes / No / Conditional | | Stable artifact IDs; Name Registry lookup for registered namespace values; Namespace G IDs where applicable; CC-PID validation for public entity IDs; no raw DB IDs exposed externally; Namespace M naming evidence for modules/components/files | G6 / G8 / G10 | Engineering Lead | |
| Architecture Governance | Material architecture, technology, or integration decision | Yes / No / Conditional | | ADRs, architecture review, deviations | G3 / G5 / G8 | Architecture Lead | |
| ERM / Risk | Material business, technology, security, privacy, vendor, or AI risk | Yes / No / Conditional | | Risk register entries, treatment decisions, acceptance records | G3 / G8 / G10 | Risk Owner | |
| Security Policy | Any software system | Yes / No / Conditional | | Security requirements, review evidence | G4 / G5 / G8 | Security Reviewer | |
| Secure Coding | Any implementation work | Yes / No / Conditional | | Coding standards, review/test evidence | G6 / G7 | Engineering Lead | |
| Auth / Identity | User, admin, service identity, sessions, login, tokens, SSO, API keys | Yes / No / Conditional | | Auth requirements/design/tests, audit notes | G4 / G5 / G7 / G8 | Security / Identity Owner | |
| AuthZ / Access Control | Roles, permissions, tenant/user ownership, privileged operations | Yes / No / Conditional | | Access-control model, policy tests, audit evidence | G4 / G5 / G7 / G8 | Security / Architect | |
| Crypto / KMS | Secrets, encryption, signing, TLS, key lifecycle, sensitive data | Yes / No / Conditional | | Crypto inventory, key/secret handling notes, review evidence | G4 / G5 / G6 / G8 | Security / DevOps | |
| Vulnerability Management | Any shipped software, dependencies, containers, infra, or third-party code | Yes / No / Conditional | | SCA/SAST/DAST results, remediation/acceptance records | G6 / G7 / G8 / G10 | Security / Engineering Lead | |
| Privacy / Privacy Handling | Personal data, tracking, consent, DSAR, cross-border processing | Yes / No / Conditional | | Privacy requirements, DPIA/assessment, consent/DSAR notes | G3 / G4 / G5 / G8 / G10 | Privacy / Legal | |
| Data Classification | Any stored/transmitted data | Yes / No / Conditional | | Data classification notes | G4 / G5 / G8 | Data Owner | |
| Data Isolation | Multi-tenant/customer data | Yes / No / Conditional | | Tenant isolation design/tests | G5 / G7 / G8 | Architect | |
| Records / Retention | Business records, audit evidence, customer/employee/financial data | Yes / No / Conditional | | Retention notes, disposal/hold considerations, evidence retention | G4 / G8 / G10 | Records / Legal | |
| Observability / Telemetry | Service, API, job, integration, production operation, tenant-scoped flow | Yes / No / Conditional | | Logging/metrics/tracing plan, dashboard/alert evidence | G5 / G6 / G8 / G10 | SRE / Engineering Lead | |
| Testing / Quality | Any implementation, release, migration, or critical workflow | Yes / No / Conditional | | Test strategy, CI evidence, coverage/defect disposition | G6 / G7 / G8 | QA Lead | |
| Release / Deployment | Any deployment, release, patch, migration, or rollback-capable change | Yes / No / Conditional | | Release plan, deployment/rollback evidence, approval record | G8 / G9 / G10 | Release Manager | |
| Change Management | Baseline, scope, requirement, design, release, or operational-impacting change | Yes / No / Conditional | | Change request, impact/risk analysis, approval/rollback notes | G4-G10 | Change Owner | |
| Vendor Risk | External vendor, SaaS, API provider, subcontractor, processor, or critical dependency | Yes / No / Conditional | | Vendor assessment, contract/DPA/security evidence | G3 / G4 / G5 / G8 / G10 | Vendor Owner / Legal | |
| AI Usage | AI-assisted or AI feature work | Yes / No / Conditional | | AI risk/use review | G3-G8 | AI / Legal Reviewer | |
| AI Engineering | AI product feature, model workflow, RAG, automated decision, evaluation pipeline | Yes / No / Conditional | | AI design review, evaluation plan/results, monitoring notes | G3 / G4 / G5 / G7 / G8 / G10 | AI Engineering Owner | |
| Clean Room Design Process | Source-reader separation, IP-sensitive rebuild, vendor handoff, litigation-safe analysis | Yes / No / Conditional | | BP-001-DRCR selection, separation log, sanitized handoff evidence | G5 / G6 / G8 | Architecture / Legal | |

---

## 5. Machine-Readable Evidence

When the project uses automation, dashboards, or audit tooling, maintain a machine-readable copy of the matrix in JSON or YAML.

Suggested JSON shape:

```json
{
  "project": "",
  "product_id": "",
  "pcl_code": "",
  "pcl_status": "candidate",
  "domain_tags": [],
  "function_descriptors": [],
  "work_type_tags": [],
  "last_reviewed": "",
  "standards": [
    {
      "standard": "Security Policy",
      "applies": "yes",
      "rationale": "",
      "phases": ["5", "7", "9", "11"],
      "gates": ["G4", "G5", "G8"],
      "evidence": [],
      "owner": "",
      "status": "planned"
    }
  ]
}
```

Allowed `applies` values: `yes`, `no`, `conditional`.

Allowed `status` values: `planned`, `in_progress`, `complete`, `waived`, `not_applicable`, `blocked`.

---

## 6. Completion Criteria

This appendix is complete when:

1. Every listed standard has an applicability value.
2. `No` and `Conditional` entries have rationale.
3. Applicable standards have named owners.
4. Evidence artifacts are named or explicitly scheduled.
5. Gate checks are acknowledged for each applicable standard.
6. Waivers, exceptions, or deviations are routed through the correct governance path.
7. The matrix is reviewed before G8 and again during G10.

# Agnostic Execution Decomposition — Create Tasks List Procedure

**Classification:** Keep — standard task-decomposition protocol for converting approved documents into five-iteration execution roadmaps, atomic tasks, and optional machine-readable task board JSON.

**Procedure ID:** TD-001

**Lifecycle placement**

| Phase | Role |
| --- | --- |
| **Phase 6 — Planning and Scope Control** | Baseline approved scope and planning artifacts; initiate or refresh the execution roadmap so scope and task granularity stay aligned. |
| **Phase 8 — Development Preparation** | Apply TD-001 to approved specs/plans/blueprints so implementation starts from an atomic, traceable backlog (`tasks_list.md`, optional `tasks_board.json`). |

**Normative references:** Master Lifecycle Phase 6 and Phase 8; USSM Tier 4 (development and test artifacts).

---

## Master Lifecycle Alignment

TD-001 is the detailed task-decomposition model used when a project needs a granular execution roadmap. In the Master Lifecycle:

- Phase 6 selects or proposes the execution decomposition model; when TD-001 is selected, it may start from approved scope, requirements, and feature inventory.
- Phase 8 finalizes TD-001 against architecture, module/file planning, environment strategy, and development readiness.
- The finalized `tasks_list.md` / `tasks_board.json` can support **G6 — Development Ready** when TD-001 is selected as the execution model.
- TD-001 may be referenced by **Template A-15 — Development Plan** as the detailed execution model; it does not replace the Development Plan unless the project explicitly records that TD-001 is serving that role.
- Use either TD-001 or HG-001 as the primary decomposition model unless a written mapping exists.

The internal TD-001 words **Iteration** and **Phase** are execution-planning terms only. They are not the same as Master Lifecycle Phases 1–14.

---

## Goal

Transform structured source documents (plans, specs, blueprints, governance docs, or any formal system documentation) into a **five-iteration**, **ultra-granular** execution roadmap using a consistent, **methodology-agnostic** hierarchy.

This procedure is not tied to SDLC, Agile, Waterfall, or any lifecycle model. It is a universal decomposition protocol for complex systems.

---

## 1. Inputs and outputs

### 1.1 Source

Any structured documentation set, including but not limited to:

- Specifications
- Blueprints
- Governance plans
- Architecture documents
- Roadmaps
- Requirement repositories
- SDLC documents (optional, not required)

### 1.2 Destination

**Primary output**

- `tasks_list.md`

**Optional** (if scale requires segmentation)

- `tasks_list_iter1.md` … `tasks_list_iter5.md`

**Optional** (automation, boards, governance consoles)

- `tasks_board.json` (or per-iteration variants), aligned field-for-field with the Markdown list.

**Traceability expectation**

- When requirements, features, designs, tests, or implementation records have stable IDs, task outputs should link to those IDs per **`24. Traceability Rules.md`**.
- At minimum, trace links should be preserved in `tasks_board.json` when machine-readable planning is used.

---

## 2. Core structural hierarchy (mandatory)

Use a strict, invariant decomposition hierarchy:

```text
Iteration (Strategic Scope Boundary)
  └── Phase (Logical Execution Segment)
        └── Milestone (Verifiable Outcome)
              └── PowerTask (Atomic Deliverable Unit)
                    └── Task (Single Executable Action)
```

This hierarchy is:

- Methodology-agnostic
- Domain-agnostic
- Lifecycle-independent
- Compatible with governance, engineering, research, or operational systems

---

## 3. File and structure rules

### 3.1 Naming rules

- Default: `tasks_list.md`
- Large scope: split per iteration (`tasks_list_iter1.md` … `tasks_list_iter5.md`)

### 3.2 Numbering logic

- **Phases:** Reset at the start of each iteration.
- **Milestones:** Continuous global numbering across all iterations.
- **PowerTasks:** Reset at the start of each iteration.
- **Tasks:** Reset at the start of each milestone.

### 3.3 Formatting integrity

- Maintain strict indentation hierarchy.
- Do not skip levels.
- Do not merge levels (for example, PowerTask ≠ Milestone).

---

## 4. Scope and granularity rules

### 4.1 Milestones

**Definition:** The smallest verifiable and auditable outcome that produces a concrete system advancement.

**Examples**

- Define governance contract schema
- Implement evidence redaction pipeline
- Establish domain boundary enforcement tests

**Not allowed**

- Vague milestones
- Non-verifiable objectives

### 4.2 PowerTasks

**Definition:** Mid-sized, single-aspect execution units (typically about two to eight hours of focused work).

**Constraints**

- One concern only
- One subsystem or artifact per PowerTask
- No multi-domain mixing
- No umbrella scope

**Example**

- Implement scorecard aggregation engine  
- **Not:** Build scoring system

### 4.3 Tasks

**Definition:** The smallest atomic, immediately executable action.

**Mandatory characteristics**

- Single-responsibility
- Verb-first
- Implementation-ready
- Less than about one hour of work
- No ambiguity or placeholders

**Examples**

- Define JSON schema validation rules
- Implement deterministic hashing function
- Add CI test for domain boundary violation

If a task takes more than a morning, decompose it further.

---

## 5. Logical workflow sequence (agnostic)

### 5.1 Analyze source documentation

- Extract domains, components, artifacts, constraints, and execution logic.
- Identify dependencies and authority boundaries.
- Detect implicit deliverables and hidden work units.

This analysis is independent of any lifecycle model.

### 5.2 Establish strategic iteration segmentation

Divide the roadmap into five progressive **capability layers** (not SDLC phases):

| Iteration | Capability layer |
| --- | --- |
| **1** | Core functional baseline (minimal viable execution) |
| **2** | Foundational expansion (stability and core features) |
| **3** | Control and governance extensions (identity, roles, constraints, and similar, if applicable) |
| **4** | Full system completion (remaining capabilities and integrations) |
| **5** | Validation, optimization, and operational hardening |

### 5.3 Define phases (logical segments)

Phases must represent **logical execution segments**, not lifecycle labels.

**Valid phase types (examples)**

- Foundations  
- Core Processing  
- Decision Logic  
- Persistence and Evidence  
- Consumption / Interfaces  
- Enforcement and Validation  
- Optimization and Hardening  

**Forbidden:** Forcing Design / Development / Testing / Deployment when not contextually valid.

### 5.4 Define and number milestones

For each phase:

- Assign a scoped title.
- Provide a one-sentence objective.
- Ensure the milestone produces a measurable outcome.
- Increment milestone numbering globally across all iterations.

### 5.5 Decompose milestones into PowerTasks

**Rules**

- Each PowerTask = one execution aspect only.
- Do not mix UI + logic + testing in one PowerTask.
- Each PowerTask must map to a tangible artifact, subsystem, or enforcement mechanism.

**Example decomposition dimensions**

- Structure  
- Logic  
- Validation  
- Enforcement  
- Integration  

### 5.6 Break PowerTasks into atomic tasks

**Task requirements**

- Fully specified  
- No implied work  
- No placeholders  
- No vague verbs (for example, “handle,” “manage,” “improve”)  
- Clear and actionable without additional clarification  

**Task ID format**

```text
<iteration>.<phase>.<milestone>.<taskNumber>
```

**Example**

```text
Task 2.3.7.1: Implement schema validation for Issues contract
```

Leave one blank line before each new block in the output file.

---

## 6. Output format (strict)

Use this plain-text structure:

```text
Iteration <iterationNumber>, Phase <phaseNumber>
Milestone <milestoneNumber>: <Milestone Title>
PowerTask <powerTaskNumber>: <PowerTask Title>
Task <taskID>: <Verb-first actionable description>
Task <taskID>: <Verb-first actionable description>
```

Where:

- `<iterationNumber>` = 1 to 5  
- `<phaseNumber>` = Sequential logical phase index (not lifecycle-bound)  
- `<milestoneNumber>` = Global incremental numbering  
- `<powerTaskNumber>` = Reset per iteration  
- `<taskID>` = `Iteration.Phase.Milestone.TaskNumber`  

---

## 6.1 Machine-readable output (JSON task board format)

**When to use:** Mandatory when automation, governance consoles, Kanban integration, or AI orchestration consumes the backlog; optional for manual planning only.

### 6.1.1 JSON file requirement

When the procedure runs in automation-enabled environments, generate a `.json` file alongside the Markdown task list.

**Recommended filename:** `tasks_board.json` (or iteration-specific variants if the Markdown is split).

### 6.1.2 Canonical schema (conceptual)

Each **list** represents a board column (for example, To Do, In Progress). Each **card** represents one task (or a minimal card with only `name` when unstructured).

```json
{
  "lists": [
    {
      "name": "To Do",
      "cards": [
        {
          "iteration": 1,
          "phase": 2,
          "milestone": {
            "number": 1,
            "title": "Foundation"
          },
          "powerTask": {
            "number": 3,
            "title": "Database Setup"
          },
          "task": {
            "id": "T-001",
            "description": "Create schema",
            "linked_requirement_ids": ["SRS-FR-001"],
            "linked_feature_ids": ["FEAT-001"],
            "linked_design_ids": ["DATA-001"],
            "linked_test_ids": ["TC-001"],
            "source_artifacts": [
              "28. Appendix A — Template Library.md#Template-A-15"
            ]
          },
          "dueDate": "2026-03-15T00:00:00Z"
        },
        {
          "name": "Simple card title"
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

### 6.1.3 Card identity rules

Each card **must** contain at least one identity source:

**Option A — Direct card title**

```json
{ "name": "Simple card title" }
```

**Option B — Task object (recommended for structured systems)**

```json
{
  "task": {
    "id": "T-001",
    "description": "Create schema"
  }
}
```

If both are present: `task.description` is the primary card title; `name` is override or fallback.

### 6.1.4 Hierarchy mapping (procedure to JSON)

| Procedure level | JSON field |
| --- | --- |
| Iteration | `iteration` |
| Phase | `phase` |
| Milestone | `milestone.number`, `milestone.title` |
| PowerTask | `powerTask.number`, `powerTask.title` |
| Task | `task.id`, `task.description` |

These fields are optional but strongly recommended for traceability.

### 6.1.5 Traceability fields

When structured traceability is enabled, include these fields on the task object:

| Field | Type | Purpose |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `linked_requirement_ids` | string array | Requirements covered by the task. |
| `linked_feature_ids` | string array | Features or scope items covered by the task. |
| `linked_design_ids` | string array | Design, ADR, API, data, UI, or module artifacts affected by the task. |
| `linked_test_ids` | string array | Test cases, acceptance scenarios, or validation evidence expected for the task. |
| `source_artifacts` | string array | Source documents/templates used to derive the task. |
| `requirements_not_applicable` | boolean | Marks technical chores that do not directly map to requirements. |
| `requirements_not_applicable_reason` | string | Required when `requirements_not_applicable` is true. |

These fields align TD-001 with **`24. Traceability Rules.md`** and support coverage checks in Phase 6, Phase 8, Phase 9, and Phase 10.

### 6.1.6 Description enrichment

When hierarchy fields are present, append them to the card description body where your tool supports rich descriptions, for example:

```text
[I1-P2-M1-PT3] Create schema
Milestone: Foundation
PowerTask: Database Setup
```

### 6.1.7 List and column resolution (board-agnostic)

- Lists match existing columns by name (case-insensitive).
- If no matching column exists, create one.
- Compatible with Kanban, governance dashboards, orchestration, and custom consoles.

**Example list names:** To Do, In Progress, Blocked, Review, Completed.

### 6.1.8 Optional fields

| Field | Type | Purpose |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `description` | string | Extended task context |
| `dueDate` | ISO 8601 UTC string | Scheduling and prioritization |
| `name` | string | Direct card title (fallback) |

**Date format:** `YYYY-MM-DDTHH:MM:SSZ` (ISO 8601 UTC), for example `2026-03-15T00:00:00Z`.

### 6.1.9 Consistency with Markdown (mandatory)

If both artifacts exist:

- `tasks_list.md` = human-readable execution plan  
- `tasks_board.json` = machine-readable structure  

They **must** stay synchronized: same iteration numbers, same milestone numbering, same task descriptions, no orphan JSON cards.

### 6.1.10 JSON requirement summary

| Scenario | JSON |
| --- | --- |
| Manual planning only | Optional |
| Automation pipelines | Mandatory |
| Governance consoles | Mandatory |
| Kanban / task board integration | Mandatory |
| AI orchestration systems | Mandatory |

---

## 7. Verification and alignment step (mandatory)

After completing each iteration:

- Compare all PowerTasks against the full source document set.
- Validate coverage of all domains, deliverables, constraints, and integrations.
- Identify missing components, hidden dependencies, or under-specified work.
- Propose precise augmentations where gaps exist.

This ensures traceability and completeness independent of any SDLC framework.

---

## 8. Forbidden practices

| Anti-pattern | Instead |
| --- | --- |
| Vague deliverables (“Build system module”) | “Define system module interface contract” |
| Multi-concern PowerTasks (UI + logic + test) | Separate PowerTasks per concern |
| Placeholder tasks (“Implement feature X”) | Specific actionable units (for example, “Implement input validation middleware for API gateway”) |
| Implied or hidden work | Explicit decomposition for every action |
| Research-only tasks without deliverables | “Document comparison of three candidate libraries with integration notes” |

---

## 9. Completion criteria

The procedure is correctly executed when:

- All source documentation is fully decomposed.
- No milestone is vague or non-verifiable.
- All PowerTasks are single-aspect and concrete.
- All tasks are atomic and executable.
- Iterations form a progressive capability ladder.
- The roadmap is methodology-agnostic and reusable across domains.
- When JSON is in scope, Markdown and JSON remain aligned.
- When traceability is in scope, task records include requirement/feature/design/test/source links or documented not-applicable rationale.
- If TD-001 supports G6, the finalized roadmap is linked from the Development Plan (Template A-15) or explicitly identified as the execution model.

---

## Related Master Lifecycle documents

- `12. Phase 6 — Planning and Scope Control.md`
- `14. Phase 8 — Development Preparation.md`
- `15. Phase 9 — Implementation.md`
- `21. Decision Gates.md` — G6 Development Ready evidence.
- `22. Required Documents.md` — TD-001 and task-board artifact registration.
- `24. Traceability Rules.md` — task traceability and stable ID rules.
- `28. Appendix A — Template Library.md` — Template A-15 Development Plan.
- `Document Decomposition — Hyper-Granular Execution Plan Directive.md` (HG-001) — alternate decomposition model using PH1–PH7 delivery phases and benchmark-centric IDs; use one primary model per program unless mapped.






# Architecture Design Document (ARD-001)

**Classification:** Phase 7 — Architecture and Design · USSM Tier 3 (DDS/SDD class) · Reference template for the **Architecture Design Document** artifact.

**Canonical ID:** ARD-001.

This artifact defines the system/software **architecture baseline** before implementation: structure, boundaries, interfaces, data, security, deployment, observability, technology choices, ADRs, and traceability to requirements. It is the primary architecture package for **G5 — Architecture Approved** and complements **`28. Appendix A — Template Library.md`** (Template A-3 DDS/SDD, Template A-11 Data Model / ERD, Template A-12 API and Integration Contract), **`UI-UX Design Document — UXD-001 Procedure.md`** when UI/UX is in scope, **`Module Design Methodology — MDM-001 Procedure.md`** when module-level design applies, and **`13. Phase 7 — Architecture and Design.md`** for phase activities, gates, blueprint extraction (**BP-001**), and UI architecture conventions.

---

## Maintenance and Regeneration

This file is the **published** ARD-001 (§1–§10, §11 project template, completion criteria). A separate **template source** exists for an optional merge script that regenerates the §11 body from a structured draft.

| Item | Location |
| --- | --- |
| **Canonical publication** | **`Architecture Design Document — ARD-001.md`** (this file) |
| **Template source** | **`sources/ARD-001-template-source.md`** — must contain the marker line `Architecture Document Template` and `⸻` section breaks expected by the script |
| **Rebuild script** | **`scripts/build-architecture-design-document-ard-001.py`** |

After editing **only** the template source, regenerate:

`python3 "Master Lifecycle/scripts/build-architecture-design-document-ard-001.py"`

For routine wording changes to the procedure or §11, edit **this file** directly. Use **template source + script** when refreshing the full §11 form or importing a new draft of the form—the script **rewrites** the merged §11 output from source; avoid running it if you have unpersisted edits here that are not reflected in the source file.

Lifecycle context: **`13. Phase 7 — Architecture and Design.md`**. Gate context: **`21. Decision Gates.md`** (**G5 — Architecture Approved**). Artifact register: **`22. Required Documents.md`**.

Draft USSM manual builds may default to **`00.Notes.md`**; pass **`--input`** to **`scripts/build_ussm_from_notes.py`** when the draft lives elsewhere (**`000.Notes.md`**, **`Universal Software Project Development Procedure.md`**).

---

## 1. Purpose

Establish a controlled technical blueprint so development is not ad hoc: major parts, communication patterns, trust boundaries, data and API architecture, security and operations views, stack choices, recorded decisions, and evidence linking architecture to requirements and validation.

---

## 2. Entry criteria

- **G4 — Requirements Approved** is recorded, including Requirements Specification Package (Template A-8), SRS (Template A-2), and NFR inputs (Template A-10 / NFR-001), or an explicit waiver exists for exploratory architecture.
- Prior-phase inputs are available to populate **Section 11** source-document references.

---

## 3. Required inputs

- Problem Definition Document (Template A-0.1), Feasibility Assessment (Template A-3.2), and Business Case (Template A-3.3) as applicable.
- Requirements Specification Package (Template A-8), CRS (Template A-1), SRS (Template A-2), NFR inputs (Template A-10 / NFR-001), Scope Document (Template A-6), and Feature Inventory (Template A-9) where maintained.
- UI/UX direction or UXD-001, constraints, compliance, security, privacy, data, API/integration, and operational notes.
- Existing repositories, diagrams, or runbooks for brownfield or migration work.

---

## 4. Activities

- Draft the Architecture Design Document using **Section 11** (template).
- Produce architecture views (context, containers, components) appropriate to project scale; align with **MOD-001** for module boundaries when decomposing.
- Record **ADRs** for material choices; map quality attributes to NFRs and validation methods.
- Route security, operations, and QA reviewers per **`05. Roles and Responsibilities.md`** and program policy.

---

## 5. Required outputs

- Completed **Architecture Design Document** (this file, Section 11).
- Sufficient traceability for **Phase 8 — Development Preparation** handoff.

---

## 6. Decision gate

- **G5 — Architecture Approved:** ARD-001, ADRs, Data Model / ERD Document (Template A-11 where applicable), API and Integration Contract (Template A-12 where applicable), UI/UX Design Document (UXD-001 where applicable), and Module/Component Design Documents are reviewed as applicable before broad implementation. Evidence must satisfy **Section 8** quality checks and **Section 11.5** completion criteria.

---

## 7. Roles responsible

| Role | Responsibility |
| --- | --- |
| Architect / technical lead | Owns system structure, ADRs, and coherence |
| Project owner | Confirms fit to goals and scope |
| Backend / frontend / database reviewers | Review respective tiers |
| Security / governance | Trust boundaries, auth, privacy, compliance |
| Operations / DevOps | Hosting, deployment, observability, readiness |
| QA / test | Testability and validation hooks |

---

## 8. Quality checks

- System **context** and **boundaries** are explicit; **trust zones** identified.
- **Containers / modules** and principal **data flows** are documented.
- **Security**, **deployment**, and **observability** are addressed—not silently deferred.
- **Technology** choices justified; **ADRs** exist for consequential decisions.
- **Traceability** links architecture elements to requirements and verification evidence.

---

## 9. Exit criteria

- **Section 11.5** completion criteria satisfied and **approval status** recorded with named reviewer and date.

---

## 11. Architecture Design Document — Template

### 11.1 Purpose (artifact)

The Architecture Document defines the technical structure of the software system before implementation begins.

Its purpose is to describe how the system is organized, what major parts it contains, how those parts communicate, what technologies are used, what data stores are required, what boundaries exist, and what architectural decisions guide development.

This document ensures that the project is not built randomly. It provides a controlled technical blueprint that developers, reviewers, testers, maintainers, and future team members can use to understand and validate the system.

This document belongs to **Phase 7 — Architecture and Design**.



### 11.2 Owner

| Role | Responsibility |
| --- | --- |
| Project Owner | Confirms the architecture supports project goals and scope |
| Technical Lead | Defines implementation structure and technology choices |
| Backend Developer | Reviews services, APIs, data access, and integration design |
| Frontend Developer | Reviews client architecture, UI integration, and state/data flow |
| Database Designer | Reviews schema, entities, relationships, and data lifecycle |
| Security / Governance Reviewer | Reviews trust boundaries, authentication, authorization, privacy, and compliance risks |
| Operations / DevOps Reviewer | Reviews environments, deployment model, observability, backups, and operational readiness |
| QA / Test Reviewer | Confirms the architecture can be tested and validated |

**Primary owner:** Architect or Technical Lead.

### 11.3 Required sections (21)

1. Project Identification  
2. Source Documents  
3. Architecture Summary  
4. Architecture Goals and Principles  
5. System Context  
6. Architecture Style  
7. System Boundaries and Trust Zones  
8. Major Containers / Applications  
9. Major Modules and Components  
10. Data Architecture  
11. API and Integration Architecture  
12. Security Architecture  
13. Deployment Architecture  
14. Observability and Operations Architecture  
15. Technology Stack  
16. Architecture Decisions  
17. Quality Attribute Mapping  
18. Risks, Constraints, and Trade-Offs  
19. Architecture Diagrams  
20. Architecture Traceability Matrix  
21. Approval Status

Helpful questions:

What is being built?
What are the major parts of the system?
Where does the frontend live?
Where does the backend live?
Where is data stored?
What external systems are involved?
What architecture style is being used?
What are the most important technical decisions?

Example:

The system will use a modular web application architecture with a React frontend, Node.js backend API, relational database, and external email service integration. The backend will expose REST APIs, enforce authentication and authorization, and store core business data in PostgreSQL. The system will be deployed to a cloud environment with separate development, staging, and production configurations.

#### 4. Architecture Goals and Principles

-

Common architecture goals:

Maintainability
Security
Scalability
Testability
Performance
Reliability
Modularity
Clear separation of concerns
Operational visibility
Ease of deployment

Example principles:

- Use modular boundaries so each major feature has a clear responsibility.
- Keep business logic separate from UI, database, and external service concerns.
- Prefer simple architecture unless complexity is justified.
- Make security and privacy part of the design, not an afterthought.
- Ensure the system can be tested at unit, integration, and acceptance levels.

Alternatives Considered:
